  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8cd5fe84-30d9-4a39-b3da-6feca358f02d'

<span id="freeTextContainer12546149590623164159"><i>Shadows of Self</i> shows Mistborn’s society evolving as technology and magic mix, the economy grows, democracy contends with corruption, and religion becomes a growing cultural force, with four faiths competing for converts.<br/><br/>This bustling, optimistic, but still shaky society now faces its first instance of terrorism, crimes intended to stir up labor strife and religious confli</span>
  <span id="freeText12546149590623164159" style="display:none"><i>Shadows of Self</i> shows Mistborn’s society evolving as technology and magic mix, the economy grows, democracy contends with corruption, and religion becomes a growing cultural force, with four faiths competing for converts.<br /><br />This bustling, optimistic, but still shaky society now faces its first instance of terrorism, crimes intended to stir up labor strife and religious conflict. Wax and Wayne, assisted by the lovely, brilliant Marasi, must unravel the conspiracy before civil strife stops Scadrial’s progress in its tracks.<br /><br /><i>Shadows of Self</i> will give fans of <i>The Alloy of Law</i> everything they’ve been hoping for and, this being a Brandon Sanderson book, more, much more.</span>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/666514-i-am-about-an-hour-into-this-book-but-to">I am about an hour into this book but to be honest I am struggling. I loved the original Mistborn trilogy, it was darker and more adult than this and the alloy of law. This and the Reckoners books seem much lighter fodder as if Brandon is aiming them at a younger audience? I would like to read the stormlight archives, please advise me if these books are closer to the Mistborn trilogy or closer to the recent books?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_666514'><a id="like_count_community_question_666514" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/666514?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">6 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16065004-shadows-of-self">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/666514-i-am-about-an-hour-into-this-book-but-to">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/666514-i-am-about-an-hour-into-this-book-but-to">See all 7 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/63866376-mcsteve"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/63866376-mcsteve">McSteve</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think you're confusing "Darker" and "Adult". I worry that you're not letting yourself enjoy some really cool books, simply because you associate two<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think you're confusing "Darker" and "Adult". I worry that you're not letting yourself enjoy some really cool books, simply because you associate two things that aren't inherently linked. If you need to read edgy books to feel mature, then you're going to miss a lot of neat stuff.<br /><br />However, the books do get darker, and Bands of Mourning in particular is several shades closer to the feel of the original trilogy. If you push through, I think you'll find yourself enjoying them more and more as you progress.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2159792036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159792036" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159792036?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473208216" href="/book/show/23848109-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=adult-fantasy-sci-fi">adult-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159792036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13464677950517238974">4.75⭐️<br/><br/>JUST HOLD THE FUCK UP. THAT ENDING! H... HOW!<br/>Leave it to Sanderson to come out of the left field and soccer punch you right in the brain! That's right, you COULD get soccer punched in the brain. It's a risk one has to take when picking up his book.<br/><br/>Honestly, I'm very hesitant to say anything so as not to run the risk of spoiling too much as his renown lies in his unexpected plot twists and intriguing-as-hell narrative turns. <br/>But what I CAN say is that the narrative begins and ends with a ba</span>
  <span id="freeText13464677950517238974" style="display:none">4.75⭐️<br><br>JUST HOLD THE FUCK UP. THAT ENDING! H... HOW!<br>Leave it to Sanderson to come out of the left field and soccer punch you right in the brain! That's right, you COULD get soccer punched in the brain. It's a risk one has to take when picking up his book.<br><br>Honestly, I'm very hesitant to say anything so as not to run the risk of spoiling too much as his renown lies in his unexpected plot twists and intriguing-as-hell narrative turns. <br>But what I CAN say is that the narrative begins and ends with a bang, people! <br>This book, simply put, is everything I've said in my The Alloy of Law review AND THEN SOME (I kinda don't want to repeat myself). <br>Sanderson takes the quality of the Mistborn trilogy, blends the magical elements with technological advancements and offers it back to us from a new Wild-West perspective, giving us the absolute best of the old, with the adventure of the new. So, to sum up, this long-winded intro, GO IN BLIND AND ENJOY THE ALLOMANTIC RIDE! <br><br>Picking up one year after TAoL, Shadows kicks off with a mystery as Wax and Wayne once again take up the role of independent Lawmen for the city of Elendel. <br>There’s a boatload of Allomantic action, divine and Cosmere-related lore, great character development, some emotion filled chapters, and - stating the very obvious here but if there's one thing Brandon Sanderson is a master of, it's world-building!<br>It continues to flesh out the wild west-styled world of Mistborn and this time around, with some unexpected appearances of familiar faces. Oh, the damn feels! Hitting me right where it hurts. AGAIN! I don't like the idea of swimming in spoiler territory so, I shall quit it while I can but suffice it to say that, emotions definitely took over... and big time.<br><br>The writing style was as engaging and immersive as all of his other books, and the characters were all pretty vibrant and well-written. <br>Wax, Wayne, and Marasi were each given a compelling journey in this book that deepened their characters and their world, as they move through a spectrum of emotion and deal with their inner demons, so to speak. <br>Wax, my dear poor, tortured-soul, Wax continued to angst the atmosphere while resident wackjob Wayne stayed true to his crazy nature by offering us some much appreciated comic relief.<br><br>Now, much like my Final Empire review, I feel like I haven't even scratched the surface so let me just turn to other means of… expression to really describe my state of mind as I was reading this:<br><br><b>So, before I started, you know... it's Mistborn. Obviously, the excitement took over...<b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498250135ra/23110200.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">...</b><br><br>And it's all rainbows and unicorns as I'm getting reacquainted with my loves…</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514082784ra/24749341.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Of course none of that lasts because, as the questions start piling up and answers are nowhere to be found, you’re slowly but surely entering that all familiar - just hold the fuck up now - territory…</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503446985ra/23664302.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457631796ra/18382641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>And then dear friends… the avalanche strikes…</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514136456ra/24753404.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Continued my buddy-read with my girl, Warda, who’s as equally obsessed with Sanderson as I am.😍<br><br>Have fun!☺️</span>
  <a data-text-id="13464677950517238974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1683776986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1683776986" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1683776986?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473208216" href="/book/show/23848109-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1683776986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14466106471447036922">These new mistborn books are essentially crime-thrillers set in the same world a few hundred years later. They work so well. We have all the world building we’re used to, and the glorious action, but we also have the tension and mystery created by hunting down an unknown assailant, an unknown foe. The result is more of Sanderson’s excellence with a very cool twist. <br/><br/><b> Explosive plot </b><br/><br/>Sanderson’s writing is concise and quick. Wax’s story is easy to become engaged in. He begins by following a series </span>
  <span id="freeText14466106471447036922" style="display:none">These new mistborn books are essentially crime-thrillers set in the same world a few hundred years later. They work so well. We have all the world building we’re used to, and the glorious action, but we also have the tension and mystery created by hunting down an unknown assailant, an unknown foe. The result is more of Sanderson’s excellence with a very cool twist. <br /><br /><b> Explosive plot </b><br /><br />Sanderson’s writing is concise and quick. Wax’s story is easy to become engaged in. He begins by following a series of clues that lead him to the corpse of the apparent criminal. But life is never that simple, murders are rarely that simple. Things become slightly more complex and murky. Elements of the original trilogy are brought in. Creatures that were supposedly mere legends are walking around killing people for undetermined reasons. This results in a rather strange case to solve because everything has become so devastatingly surreal. No one has heard from these creatures in centuries. Why are they back now? What do they want? <br /><br />Wax and Wayne have their hands full. And to make the plot even better, and Wax’s life just that little bit harder, the Gods start talking to him. Yes, the Gods. He’s not gone insane; he has merely found a secret conduit that unlocks the third system of metal magic. So yes, it’s all perfectly normal. Well it isn’t. This may seem ordinary to returning readers. But for Wax, this sort of power is ancient myth; it is legend and fable. Its resurgence makes little sense to the established world that has formed his life. Something has been uprooted: change is coming. <br /><br /><b> It’s all about Wayne </b><br /><br />The best thing about this book was the splitting of the point of views. Wax is a cool enough character, but Wayne steals the stage. He is more charismatic, adaptable and rounded. His past seems darker and his future more redemptive. All in all, he is the better written character of the two. I was glad he has more of his own narrative here. In the last book he had a minimalistic contribution. This time round the story was more dynamic and entertaining. <br /><br /> Moreover, Wayne is just a stronger person. I’d like to see him take the lead for a change or, at the very least, see more of his past. This is obviously Wax’s story, but I think a novella about Wayne would be rather perfect. I just prefer him. I think one day, when Wax finally loses it, he seems to becoming more and more unhinged, Wayne may have to put him down or at least pick him back up again. I think that would be a very strong ending to such a series. But I doubt that would happen. It would be too brutal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14466106471447036922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1410629768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410629768" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410629768?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer121251779070662277"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Ya'll, my reviews for <i>Mistborn</i> are getting repetitive <b>but in case you didn't already know I love this series with every chamber of my blackened heart.</b><br/><br/><u>This new series feels like a love letter to fans who adored the original trilogy.</u><br/><br/>There's so much here to love. These books are <b>purely additive</b> to the original, they're existence only <i>enhances</i> your experience as a reader and a fan.<br/><br/>I just can't even wrap my head around the idea that someone can have all of this magnificence ju</span>
  <span id="freeText121251779070662277" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Ya'll, my reviews for <i>Mistborn</i> are getting repetitive <b>but in case you didn't already know I love this series with every chamber of my blackened heart.</b><br /><br /><u>This new series feels like a love letter to fans who adored the original trilogy.</u><br /><br />There's so much here to love. These books are <b>purely additive</b> to the original, they're existence only <i>enhances</i> your experience as a reader and a fan.<br /><br />I just can't even wrap my head around the idea that someone can have all of this magnificence just sitting around inside them? <br /><br />If I wake up in the morning without hitting snooze I'm pretty proud of myself. I couldn't imagine being master of a creation like <i>Mistborn.</i><br /><br /><b>I don't know you guys, just officially consider me #Sanderstruck!</b><br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">this sweet angel!</a></span>

<div id="review_1409808985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409808985" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409808985?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=quit-crying-robin">quit-crying-robin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409808985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1752602033004833121">Super fast re-read with some friends at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> before Bands of Mourning. <br/><br/>Knowing the ending made certain parts of this book just heartbreaking. I love that almost every BS book I reread I enjoy just as much if not more the second time through. All the original Mistborn nostalgia was FAN-FREAKING-TASTIC!<br/><br/><b>4.5 Faceless Immortal Stars</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>The Fan Girl Part of My Review</b>
  <br/>
  <i>Deal with it he is like my FAVORITE fantasy author….but there will be a real review below this</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I am in AWE yet </span>
  <span id="freeText1752602033004833121" style="display:none">Super fast re-read with some friends at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a> before Bands of Mourning. <br><br>Knowing the ending made certain parts of this book just heartbreaking. I love that almost every BS book I reread I enjoy just as much if not more the second time through. All the original Mistborn nostalgia was FAN-FREAKING-TASTIC!<br><br><b>4.5 Faceless Immortal Stars</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>The Fan Girl Part of My Review</b>
  <br>
  <i>Deal with it he is like my FAVORITE fantasy author….but there will be a real review below this</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I am in AWE yet again that the same man who had currently undertaken the task of writing all the planned books in <a>The Cosmere</a> something like 36 books when complete, but currently 17 books strong, also wrote a superhero trilogy <a>The Reckoners</a>, something a little on the crazy side <a>Legion</a> and hey why not add in a middle grade series or two just for fun. I mean this book here wasn’t even originally planned, Sanderson was writing a novella that was supposed to keep us interested in the Mistborn world and it turned into a semi-standalone book and a trilogy.<br><br><b>I might even believe this</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444256508i/16474727._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="184" alt="shards" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And it isn’t like he is just putting out novels to put out novels. They are complete stories with intricate worlds, planned out magic systems, cohesive plots, great characters AND just to top it all off he has fantastic artwork (including maps, journal pages, armor/fashion designs, creature drawing etc….) throughout. <br><br>One of the reasons I’m gonna fangirl a little more right here is that both <b>Alloy of Law and Shadows of Self it is a brand new world even though it is a Mistborn novel</b>. BS took the events of The Final Empire and wove them into how they would have shaped society 300 years after the fact. How the stories of those days would become lore and work into religion, culture and superstition. Down to the families that survived, how alomancy is affected and how the surroundings are named. It is intricate and natural all at the same time. Honestly in my opinion BS has one of the greatest imaginative minds in the fantasy genre.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Completely Spoiler Free Section:</b>
</blockquote><br>First things first <b>Do you need to have read the original Mistborn series to read this book?</b> - <i>Technically no you don’t BUT…there are many more references to what happened in The Final Empire and while I would say that you could totally read Alloy of Law without reading Mistborn 1-3 I believe wholeheartedly that the enjoyment of this book in particular would be decreased if you hadn’t read them.</i> I actually had just finished a re-read of the first three of the series and was really glad, because I picked out so many small details added in.<br><br>The thing that I really love about Brandon Sanderson (BS) novels is that I have no trouble picturing myself in the story. He tells the story in a way that I’m shown the buildings and the surroundings, I’m given insight into the culture, religion and magic system and it is done in such a way that it is in the story and almost never feels like an info dump. This is amazing especially if you look at the size and complexity of the world he is building.<br><br>Shadows of Self like Alloy of Law is sort of a mash up of <b>Mistborn World + Steampunk + Industrial Revolution + Wild Wild West</b>. It has a lot more humor in it than The Final Empire and it feels generally lighter. The banter and humor of Wax, Wayne and Marasi is fantastic and sets the tone of the entire story. Honestly the Bromance between Wax and Wayne is my favorite in fantasy <i>slightly beating out Tyrion and Brom</i> they are hilarious on page together and actually Wayne is hilarious and scene stealer all on his own too. But don’t let that fool you there are still a few gut punching moments that really knocked me in the feelings. <br><br>Favorite Character in this book – <b>Wayne</b> <br><br>Looking through my quotes he has the most highlights. He says deep insightful things one minute and then is ridiculous the next. But I smile every time he is on page, <i>there are Wayne quotes below in the semi-spoilery review</i> but we also get to see into a deeper side of Wayne and I loved the depth it gave his character.<br><br>Favorite New Character – <b>MeLaan</b><br><br>Although it can be argued she is an old character….but semantics. She added some insight into the days just after The Final Empire ended and what became of her people. Also I really loved the way she played with the team, I hope she is a player in the next book as well.<br><br>Most Improved Character -<b>Steris</b> <br><br>Don’t get me wrong <b>I’m still completely on the Wax/Marasi ship</b> and it might take a Chasmfiend or Koloss Warlord to sink that but Steris really grew on me this book. I have always liked her and her stiff overthinking overplanning ways, hey I can relate, but she really shined in this. She isn’t like a lot of female characters in fantasy and I like the non-emotional relationship that she and Wax have and how she deals with him. She has no illusions about who or what he is and just plans around it. Honestly her last scene in this book….GAH no words really. Because I loved her in that moment and I could even see how she and Wax might become really good friends or perhaps more <b>BUT I’m sailing on the good ship MaraWax or Waxasi and there isn’t a Chasmfiend in sight yet so</b>…..sorry Steris.<br><br>The new danger is a serial killer that seems to be trying to destabilize the city and throw it into a chaos similar to the events that led up to the last big shift of power in recent history *cough* Mistborn *cough*. Wax, Marasi, Wayne and others are searching trying to figure out who is next on the hit list and prevent the city from undergoing another revolution. The perpetrator of the events is messing with Wax specifically trying to throw him off and he will need to outthink someone trickier and smarter than himself or another revolution will happen.<br><blockquote>
  <b>Semi-Spoiler Review Section</b>
  <br>
  <i>all big/real spoilers will be tagged but Quotes everywhere</i>
</blockquote><br>Where to begin??? I’m still processing my feelings about this book because that ending left me so….so….well you will know when you get there. Everyone just give Wax a virtual hug he needs it.<br><br><b>The Humor</b> is one of the things that I’ve really enjoyed about series of Mistborn books. There are so many funny instances and dialogue that I laughed so many times throughout the story.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I heard voices in my head once too, you know.”<br>“You did?”<br>“Sure. Gave me a fright. I banged my head against the wall until I went unconscious. Never heard them again! Ha. Showed ’em good, I did. If rats move in, best thing to do is to burn the nest and send ’em packing.”<br>“And the nest … was your head.”<br>“Yup.”<br><br>Steris stopped on a page in her notebook, then turned it around. There, in her neat handwriting, was a detailed agenda for their evening at the party. The third entry read, 8:17. Way into the building likely blocked by traffic. Lord Waxillium carries us up to the top floor by Allomancy, which is completely inappropriate and at the same time breathtaking. <br>He raised an eyebrow, checking his pocket watch, which he carried in his gunbelt—not his vest—to be easily dropped with his other metals. “It’s 8:13. You’re slipping.”<br><br>Regular folk, they called something after what it was. You’d say, “What’s that, Kell?” And they’d say, “That? That there’s the crapper.” And you’d reply, “What do you do with it?” And they’d say, “Well, Wayne, that’s where you put your crap.” <br>It made sense. But rich folk, they had a different word for the crapper. They’d call it a “commode” or a “washroom.” That way, when someone asked for the crapper, they knew it was a person they needed to oppress.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>The Characters</b> are three dimensional. Wax has a complicated past with his history in the roughs and trying to be both a Lord to his house and a Lawman. It’s a difficult place to be and maybe he is being pulled in too many directions one day he will have to decide who he is… An Allowmancer or Terrisman/Lord or Lawman/Pawn or Sword no wonder he is a little surly.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“What’s wrong with you lately?” Marasi demanded. “You complain about the motorcar, about me being here, about your tea being too hot in the morning. <b>One would almost think you’d made some horrible life decision that you regret deep down. Wonder what it could be.”</b> <br>Wax kept his eyes forward. In the mirror, he saw Wayne lean back in and raise his eyebrows. “She might have a point, mate.”<br>“You’re not helping.”<br>“Wasn’t intending to,” Wayne said. “Fortunately, I know which horrible life decision she’s talkin’ about. You really should have bought that hat we looked at last week. It was lucky. I’ve got a fifth sense for these things.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Wayne while usually the fun loving sort has a demon in his past that he is still trying in his own way to atone for. I liked seeing what he puts himself through in an effort to make some sort of recompense for his greatest sin. Wayne has a peculiar way of looking at the world and some of it make amazing sense while other parts of it are ridiculous. But that just makes him all the more lovable.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“I coulda delivered that, you know.…”<br>“You, she would shoot,” Wax said.<br>“Only ’cuz she likes me,” Wayne said, smiling. He’d have welcomed an excuse to go see Ranette. This night was getting darker and darker, it seemed.<br>“Wayne…” Wax said. “You know she doesn’t actually like you.”<br>“You always say that, but you’re just not seein’ the truth, Wax.”<br><b>“She tries to kill you.” <br>“To keep me alive,” Wayne said. “She knows I live a dangerous life. So, keepin’ me on my toes is the best way to make sure I stick around…”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>I’m almost hoping that he wins her heart one of these days.<br><br>Marasi didn’t get a lot of development. She is now working with the constables and Wax has tried his hardest to put some distance between them after the initial attraction that was sparked in Alloy of Law. She seems to be over her semi-hero worship of his time in the roughs though and has become more secure in herself overall. Her alomancy even came in handy a time or two in this story and I was glad to see how it could be useful in certain situations. She is extremely competent and I believe that she and Wax are a good team hence my being on the MaraWax ship. My only disappointment is that those sparks from book 1 are totally missing here as Wax is committed to the arranged marriage with Steris and Marasi is trying to have a professional relationship with him since he is supposed to marry her half-sister. I missed the sparks. : ( <br><br><b>The Tie In’s To the Original Mistborn Series</b><br><i>lots of little spoilers in this section so I’m tagging the entire thing</i><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m going to *squee* a little here because there are still Kandra!!! I wasn’t sure what happened after the events of The Final Empire and I was pretty sure I caught one or two in Alloy of Law but now there is conformation that the Kandra are still around…*happy dance*<br><br>MeLaan coming onto the scene was fantastic and I loved learning how the Kandra now live within society instead of hidden away. She was such a great addition to the story and the team. I liked how she is so different from the Kandra that we met in The Final Empire…<br><blockquote><i>MeLaan finished her beer, then dramatically held up her hand. The palm split, forming lips, which then let out a soft belch.<br>“Cheating,” Wayne said.<br>“Just using what Father gave me,” MeLaan said. “Don’t tell me you wouldn’t belch out of other body parts if you could.”<br>“Well,” Wayne said, “now that you mention it, I can make a real interestin’ sound wif—”</i></blockquote>
<br>AND we get to see TenSoon. Can I just say that I was so excited that he was still around even if he isn’t glad that his name is known.<br><blockquote><i>“I’ve read about you,” Wax said. <br>“Thrilling,” the kandra growled. “I’m so happy Sazed included me in his little book so that drunk people can curse by my name.”<br>“They … do that?” <br>“Yes.” The wolfhound growled quietly in the back of his throat. “There are … stuffed toys too.” <br>“Oh yeah,” Wax said. “Soonie cubs. I’ve seen those around.”</i></blockquote>
<br>But the remembrances of Vin mostly and Elend sometimes choked me up a bit. This was my favorite quote in the entire book and it is about Vin herself. I thought it was completely fitting of who she was.<br><blockquote><i>“What was she like? As a person, I mean.” <br>“She was strong and vulnerable all at once,” TenSoon whispered. “She was my last master, and my greatest. She had a way of pouring everything of herself into what she did. <b>When she fought, she was the blade. When she loved, she was the kiss.</b></i></blockquote>
<br>There is also a little section where Wax thinks he sees her outline in the mist…dare I hope that she is still somehow around???<br><i>The Historica, a section of the Words of Founding, said she had melded with the mists. She had taken them upon herself, becoming their guardian as they became her essence. <b>As the Survivor watched over all who struggled, Vin watched over those in the night.</b> Sometimes he felt he could see her form in their patterns: slight of frame, short hair splayed out as she moved, mistcloak fluttering behind her. It was a fancy, wasn’t it?</i><br>Please don’t just be fancy…I would love it is Vin somehow will play a part in this. Because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who better to help slay a god than dare I say it another god…who might be Vinesk <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Hoping <br><br><b>Conversations with Sazed/Harmony</b>. I’m really excited about this. It seems that he might be pushing and pulling a bit in this world as Harmony. Damn his job is hard, MeLaan explains it so well toward the end of the story when Marasi is so upset for Wax…Hell I was upset for Wax. But I’m hoping to get both sides of the story because it seems like <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harmony might have played a really big part in Lessie’s death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and how could you not have a crisis of faith after the end of SoS.<br><br>Also in the broad Sheets I caught a glimpse of the Shardpool and Hoid showed up to drive the carriage those were some cool additions.<br><br><b>SANDERSON ENDINGS KILL ME</b> - Seriously I know that I need a quiet place to finish out the last 20% of any of his books because there is no way that I can think of anything else until it is over. That holds true here as well and while it didn’t gut punch me as hard as some of his other books *cries again about the ending of The Final Empire* it still hit me pretty hard and squeezed all my emotions. At the end I wasn’t sure what I felt except sorry for Wax.<br><blockquote>
<i>Harmony does the best He can—the best possible, by the very definition. Yes, He hurt Wax. He hurt him badly. But He put the pain where He knew it could be borne.”</i><br>GAH…..this is one of those times that I’m so sad the next book isn’t already out because I just want to know all the things so badly.<br>
</blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Overall</b> - Sanderson is a master storyteller and that still holds true here. My one and only complaint is that there wasn’t a lot to do with The Set his Uncle or the Women that went missing in Alloy of Law, but I assume that he will get to all of that eventually. We all know that I’m not super objective when it comes to Sanderson or Ilona Andrews so let’s just say if he writes it I’ll read it…multiple times usually.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1763338396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763338396" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763338396?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765383853" href="/book/show/26874783-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763338396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12774218969252859947"><b>4.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I mentioned before in my Alloy of Law review that any Mistborn fans should definitely continue with Mistborn era 1.5 despite the fact it doesn't have the epic fantasy strength and grand scope like before. Well, I stand by my words and I continue to encourage you more to read them, especially after reading Shadows of Self, you'll realize even more just how damn great Sanderson is.<br/><br/>As its sequel, Shadows of Self improved A LOT upon the foundation laid down by Alloy of Law, whether it's i</span>
  <span id="freeText12774218969252859947" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br />I mentioned before in my Alloy of Law review that any Mistborn fans should definitely continue with Mistborn era 1.5 despite the fact it doesn't have the epic fantasy strength and grand scope like before. Well, I stand by my words and I continue to encourage you more to read them, especially after reading Shadows of Self, you'll realize even more just how damn great Sanderson is.<br /><br />As its sequel, Shadows of Self improved A LOT upon the foundation laid down by Alloy of Law, whether it's in terms of characters, writings, world-building or plot, everything here is just enhanced to fully entertained you from beginning to the end of the book. I should mentioned this though, I will give this book a 4 star if I haven't read the original Mistborn trilogy (which baffles me why? if you're a lover of fantasy or books in general you really should read them.) as this time, there is a HUGE amount of information and elements expanded upon the aftermath of the original trilogy. <br /><br />Now if you're like me who's a whore for nostalgia factors, you're definitely gonna love it. Even though it's tricky and dangerous sometimes to expand upon the prequel so much as some series tend to ruin themselves by milking them too much (I won't mentioned the name in case it could triggered anyone), Sanderson did it perfectly with much balance like Harmony. :p<br /><br />The plot itself now goes into the direction of Mystery-Thriller set in a steampunk-western world, now imagine this. Sherlock Holmes combined with Mistborn elements, written by Brandon Sanderson, yeah you can probably already guess how great that sounds and well, that's basically Shadows of Self in general. The plots are very interesting it will keep you flipping through those pages (I finish the book in 3 days since I began despite having a full time job.)<br /><br />Great characters and development are one of the greatest strength from the original trilogy and it continues its strength here. Wax and Wayne, Marasi and Steris are back in full throttle and their characters are explored more. Their history, relationships, interactions and development will make you care more about each and every one of them (I'm looking at you Steris, I can't believe I'm starting to like this OCD girl :D)<br /><br />Writings are excellent as usual, it's one of the reason why I always praised Sanderson. Every words he crafted in all his works draws you towards the world in the book and make you feel as if you're really there.<br /><br />Overall I give this book a 4.5/5. It's thrilling, it's fun and funny at times. Again, I can't stress this highly enough, please for any Mistborn fans, pick this series up, give this era a try at least until this book before dropping the series, you'll see why I adore it. <br /><br />Note: for spoilers reason and for the sake of not ruin your experience, I didn't mention anything from the nostalgia factors other than they exists but trust me they are insanely good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12774218969252859947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1604182295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1604182295" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1604182295?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473208223" href="/book/show/22887640-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1604182295&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1604182295" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1455585063900988305"><b>5 Faceless Immortal Stars ★★★★★</b><br/><p>
  <br/>
</p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm not Harmony's hands," Wax whispered "I'm His sword."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>*fan girl mode activated* <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425137291ra/13851816.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Like seriously, smack my ass and call me sue, what DID I JUST READ OMG DYING & HYPERVENTILATING<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478225309ra/21049264.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>Warning this review contains mass amounts of fan girling, word vomit & worship of Brandon Sanderson.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478225309i/21049265._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Okay let's be real this book is seriously awesome & I mean like the best shit ever. I honestly can't believe how long it took me to read this book, 6 months to be exact..</span>
  <span id="freeText1455585063900988305" style="display:none"><b>5 Faceless Immortal Stars ★★★★★</b><br><p>
  <br>
</p><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm not Harmony's hands," Wax whispered "I'm His sword."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>*fan girl mode activated* <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425137291ra/13851816.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Like seriously, smack my ass and call me sue, what DID I JUST READ OMG DYING &amp; HYPERVENTILATING<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478225309ra/21049264.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Warning this review contains mass amounts of fan girling, word vomit &amp; worship of Brandon Sanderson.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478225309i/21049265._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Okay let's be real this book is seriously awesome &amp; I mean like the best shit ever. I honestly can't believe how long it took me to read this book, 6 months to be exact.. How?! Why!? What?! Well let me tell you I feel like after I read the Heroes of Ages I was in a Sanderson slump for a long time, that ending it killed me, it made me depressed in real life so I'm very happy to be back enjoying his books! I loved the Alloy of Law but this book was something else, it was absolutely amazing. I literally can't believe how good this book was around the middle, I read 100 pages in 40 minutes because I couldn't stop reading, I seriously couldn't tear my eyes away it was just so <u>good</u>. I am so close to screaming &amp; squealing at the top of my lungs even thinking about it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You put dynamite in the oven, Wayne"<br>"Gotta hide a gift where nobody'll look for it."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Ahem.. excuse me now while I fan girl over my idol. Seriously, Sanderson is the king of fantasy, his ideas are so unique, his writing is perfect and fun. I literally love everything about his writing, I can't fault a thing. I love him so much I am one of his number fan girls forever &amp; always. He needs his own shrine so I can worship his godliness. I am yet to read a book of his I hate (please note I know he would never produce rubbish anyway). I will seriously be reading his series until I'm fifty and I will still be squealing &amp; jumping around like a lunatic. All hail Sanderson! <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478225309ra/21049266.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I thought after book one all the problems were solved in Elendel, well I guess after reading the ending of this book they have just started. I found this book to be very slow at the beginning I think that is another reason I struggle to read it, but as soon as it hit the middle BOOM POW BANG action, like wow, could a book be anymore exciting or action packed? Seriously I was sitting at the edge of seat, biting my nails.. It was so intense &amp; epic, but I guess you couldn't expect anything less from the king. This is gonna be a huge call but I don't give a shit, I think this series is better then the first three mistborns. Vin is my book hero and always will be but my god I really truly adore everyone in the later series and enjoy reading it more then the first three which may I add is one of my favorite series ever, this series tho with the technology, cars, guns etc is just so FUCKING epic. Like seriously I can't wait to see what happens next.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478225309i/21049267.png" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Steris folded her arms. "Oh? I suppose I should take the butler instead, then?"<br>"If you like"<br>"Becareful about that Steris," Wayne added "Wax's butlers have a tendency to explode."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>So I can't decide which character I like better I love Wayne because he is hilarious, I love Wax because he is oh so sexy and deadly, I love Steris because she is a peach &amp; I love MeLaan because she's a badass. I do however not love Marasi yet I find her annoying, boring &amp; jealous.<br><br>I also love the moral of this story that even 'good gods' can be as harsh &amp; relentless as the bad ones, it's the perfect balance.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478226396ra/21049414.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> Ok HOLD UP;<br><br><b>Now I'm about to get my spoiler pants on so if you haven't read this book. PLEASE STOP READING NOW, you really don't want this special treat of a book to be spoiled the ending is jaw dropping</b><br><br>So let's talk about Wax's past with Lessie, Lessie is Wax's one true love, who he accidentally shot in the head, it has literally damaged him as a person, so that ENDING I didn't see coming. Like wow who would have thought bleeder was his darling dearest Lessie, I felt that 'DUN DUN DUN' music was needed for this reveal lol. That twist was so fucking good I sat there and literally screamed out "oh my god Sanderson you have managed to blow my mind" everytime I pick up one of his books I find myself looking for hints etc for the big twist that's coming, damnit I never ever get it right and he blows my mind each and everytime! Im also so so soooo excited to find out how Wax will deal with this in the next book. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I killed her," Wax whispered, squeezing his eyes closed. "I killed her <b>again.</b></i>
</blockquote><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475171267ra/20691759.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>It was awesome to see TenSoon again I really loved his character in the previous installments so it was fantastic to see him make a come back.<br><br>Wayne cracks me up, I laugh out loud the whole time reading his POV, I don't think I've ever read about funnier character in my life. I LOVE HIM. I also ship him and Ranette so much, please Sanderson give Wayne a happy ending. I really enjoy when Wayne pick pockets everything and trading it for something random, eg when he pockets the cigar box for a bruised apple. LOL<br><br><i>"You found the alcohol, I see" Wax said. "How uncharacteristic."</i><br><br><i>"You'd say, "what's that, kell?" And they'd say, "that? That there's the crapper." And you'd reply, "what do you do with it?" And they'd say, "well, Wayne, that's where you put your crap." It made sense. But rich folk, they had a different word for the crapper. They'd call it a "commode" or a "washroom". </i><br><br>Wax really grew on me in this installment there was one line that stole my heart away "You are his ruin," TenSoon said. "I am his preservation." It gave me the feels, I love relentless, badass men and that's exactly what Wax is! He is now my dreamboat &amp; it's official guys I am inlove &lt;3<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402939599i/10015953._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478238737i/21050260.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478225309i/21049268.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br> <br>I have loved Steris since her first appearance in book one, I love her lists, I love her social awkwardness, I just love her. Even tho she is a secondary character she is one of my favorites and I really ship her with my baby Wax. I can't wait to see Steris shine in the next book.<br><br><blockquote><i>"I cheated, if you must know." "...Cheated?"<br>"I know you enjoy witty conversation," she said, "so I prepared earlier, writing myself a list of things I could say that you would find engaging."'</i></blockquote><br><br>I love MeLaan she is hilarious, if I didn't already ship Wayne with someone else I would love them to get together. They are like twins haha. She is so badass and mannish I love her. She is my woman crush.<br><br><blockquote><i>After a short ride, he and Marasi had walked in on these two in the middling of their belching...contest? Wax wasn't certain if it was a contest, or a matter of mutual appreciation, like two virtuosos playing their favourite songs.<br>MeLaan finished her beer, then dramatically held up her hand, the Palm split, forming lips, which then let out a soft belch. "Cheating" Wayne said. "Just using what my father gave me," MeLaan said.</i></blockquote><br><br>Also did anyone notice Hoid was a carriage driver haha, it likes where's Wally trying to spot the world hoppers from the other novels.<br><br>Okay one more thing Trell ?! Is this the new shard God thingo ? Like we already had ruin so I'm so excited to see what this new metal is and who controls this new shard. Wowser *hyperventilating*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422061194ra/13451617.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I have so much more to write but nothing is coming out coherently, it's all just word vomit. So maybe when I settle down I can write more :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478225309i/21049269.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I recommend this book to anyone who has eyes, seriously so bloody good, you should all read it now if you haven't already<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475025455ra/20671228.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The high functioning fan girl is now signing out &lt;3</span>

<div id="review_2936737014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737014" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2936737014?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473208223" href="/book/show/22887640-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✨ A ✨  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy">faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=all-the-stars-in-the-sky">all-the-stars-in-the-sky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=cross-post">cross-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936737014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4588417558730644660">How did I go about daily life <i>before</i> I read Brandon Sanderson?? I cant even remember what my life was like before these books. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“She had a way of pouring everything of herself into what she did. When she fought, she was the blade. When she loved, she was the kiss. In that regard, she was far more … human than any I have known.”</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Elendel is no longer a peaceful and prosperous city that Harmony and the Originators left behind. Society is evolving and with that comes corruption. <br/><br/>The city is on th</span>
  <span id="freeText4588417558730644660" style="display:none">How did I go about daily life <i>before</i> I read Brandon Sanderson?? I cant even remember what my life was like before these books. <br><br><b>
  <i>“She had a way of pouring everything of herself into what she did. When she fought, she was the blade. When she loved, she was the kiss. In that regard, she was far more … human than any I have known.”</i>
</b> <br><br>Elendel is no longer a peaceful and prosperous city that Harmony and the Originators left behind. Society is evolving and with that comes corruption. <br><br>The city is on the verge of a revolution that will leave distraction in it's wake. <br><br>A team once again— Wax, Wayne and Marasi — are on the hunt for the source of the unrest in Elendel — someone who is determined to make sure the city crumbles from the inside. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1582794413ra/29026170.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so glad I jumped into this immediately after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936736710" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>. What I loved about AOL has been built on in this book. I found every single piece of information about this new world so completely interesting. <br><br>And because this is Brandon Sanderson writing, I was not bored for one second. The world, the history, the religions, the politics and how everything has been working since the time of the C_ has me desperately needing more. I want to know <b>everything.</b><br><br>As in the book before this, the mystery element as well as the steam-punk-like setting was A grade. I felt like I was with them searching and looking for clues. Needing to know <i>who</i> is behind all the events. <br><br>The character development was excellent. I loved learning more about each character, their past struggles and also their hilarious interactions. <br><br><i>Shadows of Self</i> opens up with a chapter from Wax's past, from one of his first missions in the Roughs. I absolutely adored reading about young Wax and getting a glimpse of how he used to be before Lessie's death. <br><br><blockquote>“I told myself I was setting out to find adventure; I never intended to be a lawman. I think I knew, deep down, that I couldn’t change anything in Elendel. It was too big, the men in suits too crafty. Out in the Roughs, one man with a gun meant something. Here, it’s hard to see him as anything other than a relic”</blockquote><br><br>The humour and banter was even better that before. I think this mostly had to do with Wayne's exceptional POV in this one. Sanderson wrote his chapters really really good where it reflected Wayne as an individual and his crazy way of thinking but we also get to know more about him at the same time. The excitement I felt everytime it switched to his POV was unexpected as I did love him in the first book but now he is one of my favourite characters of all time. <br><br>Marasi has really grown since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936736710" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>. She's more sure of herself. I support how she doesn't take crap from Wax and watching her chase after her dream despite what anyone else thinks of her is inspiring. I honestly love her so much. <br><br>I truly adore it when an author takes a character you at first thought was insignificant or boring and give them depth you never even thought they had. Steris was that. It was so unexpected that I actually came to like her and I'm excited to see more. <br><br><br>Sanderson does this thing where he fools you into thinking that you know where the plot is heading and then he flips it around and you're left gasping in shock. I did figure out the end reveal a few minutes before it happened but that did not eliminate it's brilliance. I was still left reeling (and crying).<br><br>I started writing this review immediately after turning the last page as I am so so anxious to jump into Bands of Mourning. I can't wait to see where Sanderson is going to take me next!<br>____<br><b>My reviews for:</b><br><br><i>Era One</i><br><br>0.5 (short story): <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608045644" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eleventh Metal</a><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604499760" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606309355" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605049392" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages</a><br><br>Book 3.5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737859" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a><br><br><br><i>Era Two</i><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936736710" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a><br>Book 6: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737748" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bands of Mourning</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4588417558730644660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1909357271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909357271" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909357271?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909357271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13570896919358120641"><b>Full(ish) review now posted!</b><br/><br/>Be forewarned. This is less of a review and more of a gush session over Sanderson’s craftsmanship in building the world of Scadrial in the Mistborn books. <br/><br/>I read Alloy of Law last year and, while I liked it, I didn’t feel driven to continue reading about the exploits of Wax and Wayne. I had no idea what I was missing. While I really enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law__Mistborn___4_' title='The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alloy of Law</a> the second time I read it, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16065004.Shadows_of_Self__Mistborn___5_' title='Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadows of Self</a> by far surpassed it. This is a book I feel is on par with the rest of</span>
  <span id="freeText13570896919358120641" style="display:none"><b>Full(ish) review now posted!</b><br /><br />Be forewarned. This is less of a review and more of a gush session over Sanderson’s craftsmanship in building the world of Scadrial in the Mistborn books. <br /><br />I read Alloy of Law last year and, while I liked it, I didn’t feel driven to continue reading about the exploits of Wax and Wayne. I had no idea what I was missing. While I really enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law__Mistborn___4_" title="The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a> the second time I read it, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16065004.Shadows_of_Self__Mistborn___5_" title="Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self</a> by far surpassed it. This is a book I feel is on par with the rest of Sanderson’s Cosmere fiction in terms of depth. As my lovely friend Mary said in her review, it felt like Sanderson wrote a love letter to the fans of his original Mistborn trilogy, and I loved it so much.<br /><br />Returning to a world you love three hundred years after the events that drew you there the first time can be jarring, which I think unfairly influenced my view of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law__Mistborn___4_" title="The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a> the first time I read it. But, now that I’ve been in this brave new world built on the foundations of one I adore, I’m thrilled with what Sanderson has done here. Characters that we know and love from the original trilogy are now the figures of myth, with entire religions built around them, and it’s fascinating to read. It’s like visiting old friends, but now they’re deities instead of the humans you once laughed with. Also, there are some of these characters that live on in different ways, and getting to see them again was a lot of fun.<br /><br />I don’t really know what to say here that wouldn’t be a spoiler. But I will say that I disagree with some readers who believe that Sanderson’s weakness is his characterization. While he obviously excels in his world-building and magic systems and plot twists, he’s no slouch when it comes to crafting characters, either. I <i>connect</i> with so many of his characters. The characters in this series, Wax and Wayne and Marasi and Steris, are no exception. Wayne was my absolute favorite in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law__Mistborn___4_" title="The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>, and I still love him, but now he’s sharing that spotlight with Wax. And Steris is really growing on me. I think she might be the most honest character in the entire series. The ending wrecked me more than a little bit, but cemented my love for Steris. I’m really excited about this series. Time to dig into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18739426.The_Bands_of_Mourning__Mistborn___6_" title="The Bands of Mourning (Mistborn, #6) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bands of Mourning</a>!<br /><br />Another buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">my darling dear</a>!<br /><br />For more of reviews, as well as my own fiction and thoughts on life, check out my blog, <a>Celestial Musings</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13570896919358120641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43718887-hasham-rasool?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1624741179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17393526664551719167">'Shadows of Self' genres are fantasy, sci-fi, crime and mystery.<br/><br/>I really like 'The Alloy of Law' and 'Shadows of Self' but I think 'Shadows of Self' is a lot better than 'The Alloy of Law'.<br/><br/>I really like MeLaan.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670326248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2449175589922673689">This was every bit as good as The Alloy of Law. The whole Mistborn series really is fantastic reading! <br/><br/>Wax, Wayne, and Marasi are back on the case of another mystery. This time they need to stop an assassin from killing the governor of Elendel. To complicate matters they also have to stop the civil unrest in Elendel from boiling over into a full blown riot.<br/><br/>The story was a ton of fun. The Wild West setting is still proving highly entertaining and the story was highly addictive and engaging. It wa</span>
  <span id="freeText2449175589922673689" style="display:none">This was every bit as good as The Alloy of Law. The whole Mistborn series really is fantastic reading! <br /><br />Wax, Wayne, and Marasi are back on the case of another mystery. This time they need to stop an assassin from killing the governor of Elendel. To complicate matters they also have to stop the civil unrest in Elendel from boiling over into a full blown riot.<br /><br />The story was a ton of fun. The Wild West setting is still proving highly entertaining and the story was highly addictive and engaging. It was packed full of the action, mystery,and humour that one expects from a Sanderson read. As an added bonus we even get to meet a few more familiar faces from the first trilogy. I'm all for that sort of nostalgia! <br /><br />This ended with a few shock twists that have left me dying to read the third instalment of the Wax and Wayne adventures. <br /><br />If I have a tiny criticism it is that the promising romance of the first series fell a little flat in this one. So much so that I even pondered jumping ship! <br /><br />All in all I loved this latest Cosmere book. <br /><br />Rating: 5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note. Micheal Krammer is as awesome as always. <br /><br /></span>

          </span>
