    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409714209?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24357485-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409714209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14125595417416483551"><i>A quick re-read before the release of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18739426.The_Bands_of_Mourning__Mistborn___6_' title='The Bands of Mourning (Mistborn, #6) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bands of Mourning</a>... 26 Jan 2016 update - just as good as the first time. No. No, it was better this time.</i><br/><br/>Wow. That was hectic. Another great story by a master of fantasy. The second book in this series is just as good if not better than the first.<br/> <br/>You don’t need to think about this too much. This was written by Brandon Sanderson. Buy it. Read it. Bask in the glow.<br/><br/>The future of the city of Elendel is balancing on a knife’s edge. Someone or something is t</span>
  <span id="freeText14125595417416483551" style="display:none"><i>A quick re-read before the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18739426.The_Bands_of_Mourning__Mistborn___6_" title="The Bands of Mourning (Mistborn, #6) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bands of Mourning</a>... 26 Jan 2016 update - just as good as the first time. No. No, it was better this time.</i><br /><br />Wow. That was hectic. Another great story by a master of fantasy. The second book in this series is just as good if not better than the first.<br /> <br />You don’t need to think about this too much. This was written by Brandon Sanderson. Buy it. Read it. Bask in the glow.<br /><br />The future of the city of Elendel is balancing on a knife’s edge. Someone or something is trying very hard to push it over and start a revolution and Waxillium, Wayne and Marasi have to team up once again to stop a disaster. Unfortunately, this fight might just be out of their league, but when has that ever stopped them?<br /><br />The story is filled with great action sequences and humour and never lets up till the end. As before, the banter between the characters is top notch and I even enjoyed Steris a lot more in this than the last book. She is starting to grow on me, even though I prefer Marasi &amp; Wax together. Wayne is his brilliant, devil-may-care self with a brand of humour that is definitely unique and he still has an interesting affection for hats.<br /><br /><i>"“I need you to stay behind as we go into those slums,” Wayne said, determined to impress solemnity into his voice. “It’s not that I don’t want your help. I do. It’s just going to be too dangerous for you. You need to stay where I know you’re safe. No arguments. I’m sorry.” “Wayne,” Wax said, walking past. “Stop talking to your hat and get over here.”"</i><br /><br />Brandon Sanderson has definitely upped the stakes with a few very interesting reveals in this one. Some of them are thought provoking while others are heart-wrenching. I found myself a bit subdued after the book’s climax, as I did not see that one coming. I did love that we got to see some of the old characters from the first trilogy though, and also the conversations with Harmony.<br /><br />I leave you with my favourite quote in the book. It is one of the Guardian’s memories, about a person he loved.<br /><br /><i>"When she fought, she was the blade. When she loved, she was the kiss."<i></i><br /><br /></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14125595417416483551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>
    <b>“The law is not something holy, son. It’s just a reflection of the ideals of those lucky enough to be in charge.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>The Final Empire ★★★★ 1/2<br/>The Well of Ascension ★★★★★<br/>The Hero of Ages ★★★★ 1/4<br/>The Alloy of Law ★★★★ 1/4<br/>Shadows of Self ★★★ 1/2<br/><br/>If you look at my above ratings of the whole series so far you would notice that this is my least favorite in the mistborn series so far. The last book surprised me in a very good wa</span>
  <span id="freeText511765359486245952" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/07/14/shadows-of-self/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“The law is not something holy, son. It’s just a reflection of the ideals of those lucky enough to be in charge.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The Final Empire ★★★★ 1/2<br />The Well of Ascension ★★★★★<br />The Hero of Ages ★★★★ 1/4<br />The Alloy of Law ★★★★ 1/4<br />Shadows of Self ★★★ 1/2<br /><br />If you look at my above ratings of the whole series so far you would notice that this is my least favorite in the mistborn series so far. The last book surprised me in a very good way and maybe I had high expectations that I should not have but I think I know why I liked this less than it is predecessors.<br /><br />I didn’t read the second series after the first trilogy. In fact, it has been a couple of years since I read the original trilogy. I had forgotten many of the details and characters from that series and I thought that this book depended much on that trilogy so I was confused and I could not get into the story as much as I wanted to. Mistborn 4 was kind of a separate story and I liked that but things started to get more complicated in this book. I liked how the magic system developed in the last book but not much was added after finishing this one and that kind of left me disappointed too.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “Cleaning the wound is often more painful<br /> than the cut itself.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The writing is as good as usual and there were so many goo quotes. I never have problems with Sanderson’s writing and that is a good thing. The characters are as good as ever, I still like the main characters, Wayne is certainly a favorite but the Kandra’s in this book were an addition that I was not a big fan of. Once again, I am pretty sure that I would have enjoyed this more if I did read it after the first trilogy immediately because to be honest, there was something exciting about seeing old beloved characters mentioned or make an appearance!<br /><br /><b>Summary:</b> I think it is a good entry in the series when connected to the original trilogy. I blame myself for forgetting some of the details. The writing and characters are great as usual but I was not a big fan of the plot or the magic system development (The magic system is probably my favorite system so far in books but I hated that not much was added here). I already continued the series and loved the third book more.<br /><br />You can get more books from <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a><br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=cosmere">cosmere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2016">2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993848362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15036854154711564490"><i>"The days of heroes has passed. The stories of people breaking out of history belong to another world. We have reached an era of modernism, both louder and more silent at the same time."</i><br/><br/>"The days of heroes has passed. The stories of people breaking out of history belong to another world. We have reached an era of modernism, both louder and more silent at the same time. <br/>An author like Sanderson doesn't write bad books, and I have enjoyed everything I've read by him. But I feel like every single M</span>
  <span id="freeText15036854154711564490" style="display:none"><i>"The days of heroes has passed. The stories of people breaking out of history belong to another world. We have reached an era of modernism, both louder and more silent at the same time."</i><br /><br />"The days of heroes has passed. The stories of people breaking out of history belong to another world. We have reached an era of modernism, both louder and more silent at the same time. <br />An author like Sanderson doesn't write bad books, and I have enjoyed everything I've read by him. But I feel like every single Mistborn book is a little disappointing compared to the one before it, and that is an unfortunate trend. The fifth book is no exception. <i>The Final Empire</i> is one of my favourite books, but <i>Shadows of Self</i> is probably my least favourite Cosmere instalment.<br /><br />The first Mistborn era was epic, and most aspects of it were amazing. The second is more like “fun stories in the Mistborn universe” than an actual continuation of the spectacular storyline. And that makes this sequel trilogy seem more like a decent experiment by Sanderson.<br /><br />Still, Wax and Wayne are fun to read about, the book is fast-paced and exciting and the major revelations add to the suspense (but yes, I did call both). I will keep reading the Mistborn series with interest, but it seems like in my eyes, the Stormlight Archive will surpass it in quality by a clear mile very soon. That’s not really a bad thing either.<br /></span>

<div id="review_600432224" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600432224" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600432224?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=arcs-and-galleys">arcs-and-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600432224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15291269031313284106">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015/10/01/review-shadows-of-self-by-brandon-sanderson/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Speculative Herald</a><br/><br/>A lot of the books that I’m excited for in 2015 are actually releasing quite late this year, so as we sauntered into fall and said good bye to summer, I was getting ready to say hello to a couple of my most anticipated titles. Shadows of Self was most definitely near the top of that list. I’m a big fan of Brandon Sanderson, and I absolutely loved The Alloy of Law – probably more than all three books of the original Mistborn trilogy put together, so sm</span>
  <span id="freeText15291269031313284106" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015/10/01/review-shadows-of-self-by-brandon-sanderson/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Speculative Herald</a><br /><br />A lot of the books that I’m excited for in 2015 are actually releasing quite late this year, so as we sauntered into fall and said good bye to summer, I was getting ready to say hello to a couple of my most anticipated titles. Shadows of Self was most definitely near the top of that list. I’m a big fan of Brandon Sanderson, and I absolutely loved The Alloy of Law – probably more than all three books of the original Mistborn trilogy put together, so small wonder that I was really looking forward to this follow-up.<br /><br />If there’s one thing I can never resist, it’s a good Fantasy meets Western setting. Three centuries after the events at the end of The Hero of Ages, the world of Mistborn has transformed into something altogether different. We’re on the cusp of an era similar to the industrial revolution, and all around are new inventions giving rise to mild hints of steampunk. On the outskirts of the built-up city of Elendel is a dusty, lawless territory known as the Roughs, where our protagonist Lord Waxillium Ladrian made his name as a lawman-for-hire.<br /><br />Magic, however, is alive and well. Allomancy and Feruchemy are still around, though applied here in a different way which preserves the marvel of the original system while adding a whole new dimension to it at the same time. Characters from the original trilogy like Vin, Elend, Kelsier and Sazed are also now long gone but not lost, their names immortalized forever in history and religion. It’s therefore possible to read this subseries without having to start with the first three books, though the experience might be richer if you do because then you’ll understand all the references to these past people and events. And for those who enjoyed the original trilogy, The Alloy of Law and Shadows of Self will introduce you to a fresh start featuring great new characters in a dynamic world that evolves with time. You’ll still be getting all the good stuff, but these books are far from being just the same-old, same-old; they’re shorter, more lighthearted and fun in tone and style, and I found that the mix of old and new worked very well for me.<br /><br />Shadows of Self continues the adventure by bringing back Waxillium and his good friend Wayne in a new mystery involving a hunt for an assassin. Nearly two decades have passed since Wax first started his youthful escapades into the Roughs, and he has recently returned to the city in order to take up the mantle of his lordship, which comes with a whole new set of responsibilities – including getting married. Wax and Wayne now use their allomantic powers to assist the constabulary of Elendel, working alongside the constable-general’s chief aide Marasi Harms, who is also the half-sister of Wax’s fiancée. Their latest case involves a massacre at an auction organized by the governor’s corrupt brother, whose body was found among the victims which included nobles as well the city’s most notorious crime lords.<br /><br />It soon becomes clear that the governor himself is a target. And to make matters worse, Wax learns that the assassin they hunt may not be human at all, but a Faceless Immortal who calls herself Bleeder, a kandra that ingests the bones of other beings to take on their physical appearance and personality. What do you do when your quarry could be anyone?<br /><br />Given how much I enjoyed The Alloy of Law, I was not surprised that I had a great time with this book too. Shadows of Self features a more complex plot, drawing heavily upon the world of Mistborn and its religious lore. The gods play a much bigger role in this one, with the stormy politics of the deities mirroring the political state of the mortal world. Just as the people of Elendel are sick and tired of the corruption in the government and in the nobility, not all kandra are content with Harmony’s rule. When both situations come to a boiling point, the results aren’t pretty. For readers though, it’s a tense race against time with Wax, Wayne and Marasi as they try to prevent the city from tearing itself apart, and the only way to stop the destruction is to catch Bleeder. For a supposedly insane killer, she proves to be much craftier than anyone could imagine.<br /><br />Wax and Wayne are also as fantastic a duo as the synergy of their names imply (though in truth, any scene with Wayne in it is automatically awesome, even when he’s solo) and having Marasi back is great as well. It’s interesting to see the dynamics play out between them when they work together, and as always I love the humor and the snappy dialogue which is way more prominent here than in the original trilogy, and probably where the lighter “fluffier” feel of these books comes from. Each character also has his or her own strengths and foibles, and I thought this installment explored those traits and covered them remarkably well without taking away from the main story.<br /><br />The most exciting moments came at the end for me, and I won’t lie, I was a bit of an emotional wreck after last few chapters. Strangely, I wouldn’t say the events leading up to the climax were entirely unpredictable, though the twists were a mix of “Okay, I saw that coming” along with “Wait, that wasn’t what I expected.” Either way, Sanderson knows how to deliver a conclusion, and it’s a jaw-dropping one that left me reeling from the impact. I’ve become deeply invested in Wax’s story over the course of these two novels, and the ending did not disappoint.<br /><br />All told, this book sees Brandon Sanderson doing more of what he does best – telling captivating stories that delight and enchant. Shadows of Self is another great addition to the Mistborn sequence, and another fantastic book from an author well known for his creative world-building and ingenious magic systems.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15291269031313284106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1107803328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107803328" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107803328?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473208216" href="/book/show/23848109-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107803328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11484908284048010542">Totally almost forgot to review this but better late than never so here goes! <br/><br/>I was very excited about the release of this book (although no where near as excited as I will be for Calamity or Stormlight #3) as I hadn't had any fresh Sanderson for a while and with this being the return to the Mistborn world I was hoping for a good story. This is certainly a likeable story, but for me I kind of hoped for a little more from Sanderson, and whilst I appreciate that this is a new 'era' of Mistborn, I </span>
  <span id="freeText11484908284048010542" style="display:none">Totally almost forgot to review this but better late than never so here goes! <br /><br />I was very excited about the release of this book (although no where near as excited as I will be for Calamity or Stormlight #3) as I hadn't had any fresh Sanderson for a while and with this being the return to the Mistborn world I was hoping for a good story. This is certainly a likeable story, but for me I kind of hoped for a little more from Sanderson, and whilst I appreciate that this is a new 'era' of Mistborn, I kind of loved the big epic scale of the previous series and this doesn't really compare.<br /><br />Let me begin this by saying I was excited for this, but not massively-hyper-dying-excited because I didn't 'love' the Alloy of Law, which is the introduction to these characters. I thought that Alloy of Law was fun and entertaining, but I didn't think it really captured my attention or interest as much as the original Mistborn trilogy despite bringing new ideas and magic to a world I already knew and loved.<br /><br />My biggest complaints with this book are that I feel it's probably a bit too predictable (at least I worked out what the 'twist' was before it happened which was a little annoying) and it's a lot faster paced than many f Sanderson's other adult Cosmere books. I personally love to get deep into a world and story and really connect with the characters and what's happening with them, but in this book I just couldn't fully connect because I didn't want to be reading about these 'roguish' characters, I much preferred the original cast of characters. I think that because this is such a fast paced book and is filled with mystery elements and quick, funny conversation I just couldn't fully immerse myself like I did with the first series where the mystery is ongoing for all three books. I know that this is by no means the 'end' of the series and that there's still two books to go (which I will still buy of course) but this one just didn't pull me in as much as I wanted. <br /><br />The story is once more focused on the characters of Wax and Wayne and I have to say that Wax is good, but Wayne is far superior as a character to me. He is funny, sarcastic and full of some hilarious punchlines and moments which kept me enjoying the book throughout. I do like Wax as a character, but he certainly seems a little too 'boring' in comparison with Wayne who was just on top form for most of this book.<br /><br />I do appreciate what Sanderson is aiming for with this series in terms of following the progression of a world throughout time, but I just wish the books had stayed with a longer page length and been a little more through and developed. I think that the ideas Sanderson voices about Religion (there's A LOT of religion in this book btw) and the way that it's perceived and the way people think of it is interesting, but at points it did feel a little forced even for me (a long-term Sanderson fan and someone who likes to see religion and magic systems created by him). <br /><br />On the whole the story is fun, but nothing more for me. However, I did read this with a lot of other people and they all seemed to love it so it may well be that this period of history just isn't working so well for me. I know Sanderson was prepared to lose some of his fans with this series as it was rather different, and I think maybe I am one of those who just doesn't like this anywhere near as much as the original, but I know a ton of people who do so it may well still be worth reading. I will say if you didn't care for the Alloy of Law then this is fairly similar in style etc so maybe not to read it if that's the case, but it's a fun story and although I had some frustration with parts of it it's not a poorly written or un-engaging story and I got through it in a day! :) <br />A 3* overall, fun, likeable, but by no means the best Sanderson I've read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11484908284048010542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966838496" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18133818709851487315"><b>4.5</b><br/>But honestly, it's a 5 stars!<br/><br/>Sweet potatoes and carrots sticks!<br/>Why did it take me this long to read this?! I mean on one hand, I’m glad bc I lost my faith in some of the Cosmere books and this restored it, but on the other hand… Actually you know what there is no other hand, I’m glad I took this long to read it.<br/><br/>I wanna say that there are some things I didn’t like and others that fell short to me. I predicted most things here, and Sanderson said that he wrote most of it before Wheel of Time an</span>
  <span id="freeText18133818709851487315" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b><br />But honestly, it's a 5 stars!<br /><br />Sweet potatoes and carrots sticks!<br />Why did it take me this long to read this?! I mean on one hand, I’m glad bc I lost my faith in some of the Cosmere books and this restored it, but on the other hand… Actually you know what there is no other hand, I’m glad I took this long to read it.<br /><br />I wanna say that there are some things I didn’t like and others that fell short to me. I predicted most things here, and Sanderson said that he wrote most of it before Wheel of Time and the last parts after finishing it and you can tell that he did, some of the things feel like he wrote them on the spur of the moment.<br /><br />With that said this was A LOT OF FUN! I haven’t enjoyed a book like I did this in a loooong time, besides the magic and the western/sherlock thing going on, it’s finally the witty, I repeat, WITTY, and funny, I repeat, FUNNY, characters I been wanting to read about unlike some others, and I don’t wanna name names, ahem ahem, Shallan from Stormelight!!!!<br />Anyway let’s not go there and by there I mean hell cuz that’s were Shallan deserves to be.<br />Okay okay I needed to say it, now I’m done 🙂<br /><br />So yeah, I’ll be honest and say that 80% of the reason I enjoyed this is my awetastazing friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a>, the girl is insanely awesome!<br /><br />The book tho is also awesome, it’s that it made me think, it’s that it made me do my research and connect the dots to other Cosmere books, and the fact that it took an already amazing magic system and said what if!<br />I loved the characters and the plot, but all that is bc I take them and try to figure out how could they play a role in the bigger picture. All this came very late in the book tho, and what triggered it was the pain at the end, I saw it coming, I felt it sneaking in like the mist on a cold night and I embarrassed it. <br /><br />So yeah I remember how Sazed questioned his faith in the first trilogy and I love love that it’s happening here to other characters. And I wanna say here that so far, with not many details, I like where all the characters are heading and personally I find this way more interesting than Kaladin in Stormlight, I actually wished Kal would go thru something like this but I dunno why Sanderson is too easy on him 🙂<br />I loved the romance and this is a first in a Cosmere book since Era 1! Holly heck give me more Wax and Steris. Give me Wayne and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[MeLaan <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Give me all the characters and all the chips! I’m all in! Pun intended!<br /><br />Is it weird that I loved the Ars Arcanum in this book? I feel like there’s a lot to unravel there and I wanna know more, definitely reading White Sand soon!<br /><br />Yes this was my rant, I’m finally happy I read this and with all its flaws I had so much fun! My only complaint would probably be that the fun ended quickly, and also didn’t like how Marasi and Aradel handled the things at the end, I didn’t like them pretending to be nice and know what’s best for city ,even tho they are and do, still I wished things go outta hand bc I’m evil like that 🙂<br /><br />----------------------------------------------------<br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r" rel="nofollow noopener">The thorn in my side and the spear thru my heart</a></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1413084451?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1413084451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9539622523568162558"><i>No, freedom was not lack of responsibilities—it was being able to do what was right, without having to worry if it was also wrong.</i><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438192957ra/15676197.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Dammit Sazed!!!!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445267277ra/16623034.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><br/>Now that I've gotten that out of my system, let's get on with the review (well I'm gonna call this review, even though I have no idea in what it will turn out to be).<br/><br/>This book. This <b>damn</b> book. After I've finished <i>Alloy of Law</i> I had very high expectation for this book, and now I can safely say that it exceeded every single</span>
  <span id="freeText9539622523568162558" style="display:none"><i>No, freedom was not lack of responsibilities—it was being able to do what was right, without having to worry if it was also wrong.</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438192957ra/15676197.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dammit Sazed!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445267277ra/16623034.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br>Now that I've gotten that out of my system, let's get on with the review (well I'm gonna call this review, even though I have no idea in what it will turn out to be).<br><br>This book. This <b>damn</b> book. After I've finished <i>Alloy of Law</i> I had very high expectation for this book, and now I can safely say that it exceeded every single one of my expectations. It was just <b>that</b> good. I'm still positive that Sanderson can't write a novel that isn't amazing.<br><br>I've got to say that my favorite thing about <i>Shadows of Self</i> is that, even it had completely different tone from original Mistborn trilogy, I still felt like I was reading an original Mistborn novel, and that brought a lot of feelings of nostalgia. Every time an original character was mention, I felt like I was going to do a mix of crying and laughing.<br><br>And the characters were amazing as always. I don't think I've disliked any of the characters in this books (well now that I've think about it, there are few exceptions). Wayne still remains my favorite character, and that is why I'm afraid that something bad will happen to him later on. Sanderson, for the love of God, do not kill him!!<br><br>And then, finally, the ending came and left me completely destroyed. It's not quite as emotional as Hero of Ages, but it was still emotional as hell. Sanderson sure loves to play with our feelings.<br><br>In conclusion, if you've read The Mistborn series and for some reason haven't decided to pick this series up, you're really missing out. Like I've said, this series isn't quite as good as the original Mistborn series, but it still is <i>pretty damn close</i>. Now all that's left is to wait for the next one to come out. January, please hurry up.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1410780050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410780050" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410780050?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=dr-reading-challenge">dr-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410780050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2352342866396073456"><b>Jan 2016: Audiobook reread before release of Bands of Mourning.</b><br/><br/>Yep, still 4.5 stars rating after reread (rounded up because Sanderson-DUH!); only because it didn't feel as epic as the initial Mistborn trilogy. This is a very personal story that we have here in Shadows of Self (I guess that's kind of alluded to in the very title of the book), particularly for Wax. It started with a Prologue which is seemingly out of the left field but really fun, and as you progress towards the end you try to bra</span>
  <span id="freeText2352342866396073456" style="display:none"><b>Jan 2016: Audiobook reread before release of Bands of Mourning.</b><br /><br />Yep, still 4.5 stars rating after reread (rounded up because Sanderson-DUH!); only because it didn't feel as epic as the initial Mistborn trilogy. This is a very personal story that we have here in Shadows of Self (I guess that's kind of alluded to in the very title of the book), particularly for Wax. It started with a Prologue which is seemingly out of the left field but really fun, and as you progress towards the end you try to brace for it but still find yourself whimpering from a sucker punch to the gut. <br /><br />Wayne has his moments too of course, and the one that sticks to you is how he is able to muster up the courage to face up to his egregious mistake all those years ago every single month. I had great fun with his impersonations which were brought to life very well by the narrator, Michael Kramer. <br /><br />While Marasi did nothing to endear me to her (I was frankly quite bored with a few of her sections), Steris' star really shone even though she was still pretty much a secondary character. She is becoming my favourite female character in Sanderson's books and I really hope to see more of her in Bands of Mourning. <br /><br />Aside from the characters, old and new <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harmony and kandras!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I love the whimsical touches of worldbuilding Sanderson incorporated into this era of Mistborn in the form of the broadsheet-interludes. He even slipped in a great tidbit for Cosmere fans here (only if you read all published Cosmere books) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After Chap 15, broadsheet article on Visitors from other Worlds - <i>That's when I came upon a mountain pool of the most perfect blue, fed by the melting snows of the heights. </i> - that HAS got to be Shardpool! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One of the best parts of this book was the more omnipresent reminders of the legacy and doctrine left behind by the characters that we have read and loved in the initial Mistborn trilogy, which was quite absent in Alloy of Law. <br /><br />A couple more days before the release of Bands of Mourning, and I am rightfully dying of anticipation. <br /> <br />------------------------------<br /><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I'm only able to write a short review for now due to a combination of jet lag and reading this through many bleary-eyed moments on the plane. Great book with a relevant socio-economic and religious intertwined plotline, interesting and amazing characters and a reveal at the end that hits you right in the gut. A lot more references to the characters of the original Mistborn trilogy that bring back poignant memories. <br /><br />Hope to write a more detailed review, probably after a quick reread to prep for Bands of Mourning come Jan 2016.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2352342866396073456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25408730-shadows-of-self">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98245866-anna-bran-san-stan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/98245866-anna-bran-san-stan?shelf=have-or-will-reread">have-or-will-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3534376952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10903672137614535292"><b>What a journey! Fast-paced, whiplash-inducing, and – a rarity for me – tearful as well. People have ventured (pun intended 😋) this tetralogy of the Mistborn series is not as good as the initial trilogy – but it really is; it is just different.</b> And yes, after reading this second installment (Mistborn #5), I admit I have to amend my own assessment: <b>It is just as brilliant and amazing, imaginative and creative. It’s the tone that sets them apart.<br/><br/>Where Kelsier, Vin and Elend‘s story was defined by t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10903672137614535292" style="display:none"><b>What a journey! Fast-paced, whiplash-inducing, and – a rarity for me – tearful as well. People have ventured (pun intended 😋) this tetralogy of the Mistborn series is not as good as the initial trilogy – but it really is; it is just different.</b> And yes, after reading this second installment (Mistborn #5), I admit I have to amend my own assessment: <b>It is just as brilliant and amazing, imaginative and creative. It’s the tone that sets them apart.<br /><br />Where Kelsier, Vin and Elend‘s story was defined by the apocalyptic setting, where bleakness prevailed which tugged on all my heart strings, Wax, Wayne and Marasi’s story is often delightfully humorous</b>; mostly thanks to witty dialog and Wayne’s hilarious character. (As a sucker for language, Wayne’s talent at imitating dialects is also a frequent source of my joy.) However, in contrast to <i>Alloy of Law</i> (Mistborn #4), <i>Shadows of Self</i> <b>regains more urgency and left me even more emotionally invested</b> (hence the tears) which makes it such a delicious combination. <b>I'm again happily unhappy.</b><br /><br />As mentioned before, <i>Shadows of Self</i> is especially fast-paced; <b>there’s no stopping this narrative freight train</b>, thanks in large part to Sanderson's creation of Wax‘s sharp character with his observational/detective skills. <br /><br />In short, I still absolutely live and breathe for this world of Allomancy, Feruchemy and Hemalurgy. (Yes, 300 years after the events in <i>Hero of Ages</i> (Mistborn #3), the latter is back to playing a major role. Which is awesome.) <b>Brandon Sanderson has confirmed his status as literary genius/god and I shall worship at his altar for all eternity.</b><br /><br />A few quotations to provide you with a glimpse into Wayne’s mind (and illustrate the difference in tone to the initial trilogy:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Wayne, are you drunk? It ain’t even noon yet!”<br />“I ain’t drunk, “ Wayne said, sniffling, “I’m investigatin’ alternative states of sobriety.”<br /><br />Spectacles. They were kind of like a hat for smart people.<br /><br />[The girls’ dormitory] looked an awful lot like a prison: three stories of small windows, stonework architecture, and iron grates that seemed to say “Stay away, boys, if you value your nether parts.”<br /><br />“You!”<br />“Hello,” Wayne said.<br />“How did you get by campus security?” . . . The tyrant rumbled around the side of her desk. It was like watching an ocean liner try to navigate the city canals. She wore a tiny hat, in an attempt at fashion. She liked to consider herself a part of Elendel upper society, and she kind of was. In the same way that the blocks of granite that made up the steps to the governor’s mansion were part of civic government.<br />“You,” she said, spearing Wayne in the chest with a finger. “I thought I told you not to come back.”<br />“I thought I ignored you.”<br />“Are you drunk?” She sniffed at his breath.<br />“No,” Wayne said. “If I were drunk, you wouldn’t look nearly so ugly.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>If you’re still not (thinking of) reading this, please check out my reviews of the previous books for some more context and let me persuade you, for your own good 😉.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3449481470?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire (Mistborn #1)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3489038784?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension (Mistborn #2)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3502744333?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages (Mistborn #3)</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3527058097?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law (Mistborn #4)</a><br /><br />Happy reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10903672137614535292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_233649'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233649.The_Great_Hunt"><img alt="The Great Hunt (The Wheel of Time, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1437870280l/233649._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3SJ7cg6nZCmwbvXzXGunBjndN0xDJoO8bx7kvaCLN0/lRFOU2MRlO8voVuOuGzXHD9f9Ae5jDlTOUDSnwgFv7w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FKaRVnc6RL2TidrP/TbgnGo6D9BwiXbIF3DUj1cx4tYswLmwoVlFr+gPed8PRnJdXDDFnd3M+yC2PgSVNbu6dg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">About Brandon Sanderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1394044556p3/38550.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">Brandon Sanderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
154,141
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14473951770750922653">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText14473951770750922653" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14473951770750922653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
